Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The previous implementation achieved a 0.87x speedup but still needs optimization. I'll improve performance by using the analytical solution for state-space systems with eigenvalue decomposition, which avoids expensive matrix exponentials for each time step:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize state and output
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = C @ x + D * u[0]
        
        # Precompute eigenvalue decomposition
        try:
            lam, V = np.linalg.eig(A)
            invV = np.linalg.inv(V)
            temp = invV @ B  # Precompute for efficiency
            use_eig = True
        except np.linalg.LinAlgError:
            use_eig = False
        
        # Cache for discretization matrices
        cache = {}
        
        # Iterate through time intervals
        for i in range(len(t) - 1):
            dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Skip computation for zero time step
            if dt <= 0:
                yout[i+1] = yout[i]
                continue
            
            # Create cache key for this time step
            cache_key = (dt,)
            
            # Compute or retrieve discretization matrices from cache
            if cache_key in cache:
                F, G1, G2 = cache[cache_key]
            else:
                if use_eig:
                    # Compute using eigenvalue decomposition
                    F_diag = np.exp(lam * dt)
                    F = V @ np.diag(F_diag) @ invV
                    
                    # Compute integral terms
                    J0 = np.where(np.abs(lam) > 1e-10, 
                                 (np.exp(lam * dt) - 1) / lam,
                                 dt)
                    J1 = np.where(np.abs(lam) > 1e-10,
                                 (np.exp(lam * dt) - 1 - lam * dt) / (lam**2),
                                 dt**2 / 2)
                    
                    term0 = V @ (J0 * temp)
                    term1 = V @ (J1 * temp)
                    G1 = term0
                    G2 = term1
                else:
                    # Fallback to matrix exponential
                    M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
                    M[:n, :n] = A * dt
                    M[:n, n] = B * dt
                    M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
                    M[n, n+1] = 1
                    
                    from scipy.linalg import expm
                    expM = expm(M)
                    F = expM[:n, :n]
                    G1 = expM[:n, n]
                    G2 = expM[:n, n+1]
                
                cache[cache_key] = (F, G1, G2)
            
            # Update state
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            yout[i+1] = C @ x + D * u1
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The eigenvalue decomposition approach introduced numerical inaccuracies. Let's revert to the best-performing version (0.87x speedup) and optimize it further by using a more efficient caching strategy and precomputing for common time steps:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}  # Cache for matrix exponentials
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize state and output
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = C @ x + D * u[0]
        
        # Precompute unique time steps
        dts = [t[i+1] - t[i] for i in range(len(t)-1)]
        unique_dts = set(dts)
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            if dt <= 0:
                continue
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = expm(M)
            F = expM[:n, :n]
            G1 = expM[:n, n]
            G2 = expM[:n, n+1]
            self.cache[dt] = (F, G1, G2)
        
        # Iterate through time intervals
        for i in range(len(t) - 1):
            dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Skip computation for zero time step
            if dt <= 0:
                yout[i+1] = yout[i]
                continue
            
            # Retrieve precomputed matrices
            F, G1, G2 = self.cache[dt]
            
            # Update state (accounts for linear input variation)
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            yout[i+1] = C @ x + D * u1
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The speedup remains similar to the previous version. To achieve a significant performance improvement, I'll implement a parallelized solution using JAX. This leverages hardware acceleration (GPU/TPU) and just-in-time compilation for optimal performance:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from scipy import signal
from jax import lax

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = jnp.array(problem["u"])
        t = jnp.array(problem["t"])
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        A = jnp.array(A)
        B = jnp.array(B.flatten())
        C = jnp.array(C.flatten())
        D = D.item() if hasattr(D, 'size') and D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Create JIT-compiled function for the main computation
        @jax.jit
        def compute_output(A, B, C, D, u, t):
            n = A.shape[0]
            x = jnp.zeros(n)
            yout = jnp.zeros(len(t))
            yout = yout.at[0].set(C @ x + D * u[0])
            
            def body_fun(i, state):
                x, yout = state
                dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # Create augmented matrix
                M = jnp.zeros((n+2, n+2))
                M = M.at[:n, :n].set(A * dt)
                M = M.at[:n, n].set(B * dt)
                M = M.at[n, n+1].set(1.0)
                
                # Compute matrix exponential
                expM = jax.scipy.linalg.expm(M)
                F = expM[:n, :n]
                G1 = expM[:n, n]
                G2 = expM[:n, n+1]
                
                # Update state
                x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
                yout = yout.at[i+1].set(C @ x + D * u1)
                return (x, yout)
            
            # Process all time steps in parallel
            _, yout = lax.fori_loop(0, len(t)-1, body_fun, (x, yout))
            return yout
        
        # Execute the JIT-compiled computation
        yout = compute_output(A, B, C, D, u, t)
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The JAX implementation introduced numerical inaccuracies. Let's return to the best-performing version (0.87x speedup) and optimize it further by using a more efficient matrix exponential computation method. We'll use the scaling and squaring method with Pade approximation, which is faster than scipy's expm for small matrices:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}  # Cache for matrix exponentials
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize state and output
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = C @ x + D * u[0]
        
        # Precompute unique time steps
        dts = [t[i+1] - t[i] for i in range(len(t)-1)]
        unique_dts = set(dts)
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            if dt <= 0:
                continue
                
            # Create augmented matrix
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            
            # Compute matrix exponential using optimized method
            F, G1, G2 = self._expm(M, n)
            self.cache[dt] = (F, G1, G2)
        
        # Iterate through time intervals
        for i in range(len(t) - 1):
            dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Skip computation for zero time step
            if dt <= 0:
                yout[i+1] = yout[i]
                continue
            
            # Retrieve precomputed matrices
            F, G1, G2 = self.cache[dt]
            
            # Update state (accounts for linear input variation)
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            yout[i+1] = C @ x + D * u1
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    def _expm(self, M, n):
        """Optimized matrix exponential using scaling and squaring with Pade approximation"""
        # Scale matrix to reduce norm
        norm = np.linalg.norm(M, np.inf)
        scale = max(0, int(np.ceil(np.log2(norm))) if norm > 0 else 0
        M_scaled = M / (2**scale)
        
        # Pade approximation (order 6)
        I = np.eye(M.shape[0])
        M2 = M_scaled @ M_scaled
        M4 = M2 @ M2
        M6 = M4 @ M2
        U = M_scaled @ (M6 + 16380*M4 + 40840800*M2 + 6915585600*I)
        V = M6 + 16380*M4 + 40840800*M2 + 6915585600*I
        expM = np.linalg.solve(V - U, V + U)
        
        # Squaring
        for _ in range(scale):
            expM = expM @ expM
        
        # Extract relevant matrices
        F = expM[:n, :n]
        G1 = expM[:n, n]
        G2 = expM[:n, n+1]
        return F, G1, G2

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}  # Cache for matrix exponentials
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize state and output
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = C @ x + D * u[0]
        
        # Precompute unique time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = set(dts)
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            if dt <= 0:
                continue
                
            # Create augmented matrix
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            
            # Compute matrix exponential using optimized method
            F, G1, G2 = self._expm(M, n)
            self.cache[dt] = (F, G1, G2)
        
        # Iterate through time intervals
        for i in range(len(t) - 1):
            dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Skip computation for zero time step
            if dt <= 0:
                yout[i+1] = yout[i]
                continue
            
            # Retrieve precomputed matrices
            F, G1, G2 = self.cache[dt]
            
            # Update state (accounts for linear input variation)
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            yout[i+1] = C @ x + D * u1
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    def _expm(self, M, n):
        """Optimized matrix exponential using scaling and squaring with Pade approximation"""
        # Scale matrix to reduce norm
        norm = np.linalg.norm(M, np.inf)
        scale = max(0, int(np.ceil(np.log2(norm))) if norm > 0 else 0
        M_scaled = M / (2**scale)
        
        # Pade approximation (order 6)
        I = np.eye(M.shape[0])
        M2 = M_scaled @ M_scaled
        M4 = M2 @ M2
        M6 = M4 @ M2
        U = M_scaled @ (M6 + 16380*M4 + 40840800*M2 + 6915585600*I)
        V = M6 + 16380*M4 + 40840800*M2 + 6915585600*I
        expM = np.linalg.solve(V - U, V + U)
        
        # Squaring
        for _ in range(scale):
            expM = expM @ expM
        
        # Extract relevant matrices
        F = expM[:n, :n]
        G1 = expM[:n, n]
        G2 = expM[:n, n+1]
        return F, G1, G2

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the syntax error in my custom expm implementation. Let me fix it and also optimize the code further by using the analytical solution for state-space systems with eigenvalue decomposition, which avoids expensive matrix exponentials:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize state and output
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = C @ x + D * u[0]
        
        # Precompute eigenvalue decomposition
        try:
            lam, V = np.linalg.eig(A)
            invV = np.linalg.inv(V)
            temp = invV @ B  # Precompute for efficiency
            use_eig = True
        except np.linalg.LinAlgError:
            use_eig = False
        
        # Cache for discretization matrices
        cache = {}
        
        # Iterate through time intervals
        for i in range(len(t) - 1):
            dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Skip computation for zero time step
            if dt <= 0:
                yout[i+1] = yout[i]
                continue
            
            # Create cache key for this time step
            cache_key = dt
            
            # Compute or retrieve discretization matrices from cache
            if cache_key in cache:
                F, G1, G2 = cache[cache_key]
            else:
                if use_eig:
                    # Compute using eigenvalue decomposition
                    F_diag = np.exp(lam * dt)
                    F = V @ np.diag(F_diag) @ invV
                    
                    # Compute integral terms
                    J0 = np.where(np.abs(lam) > 1e-10, 
                                 (np.exp(lam * dt) - 1) / lam,
                                 dt)
                    J1 = np.where(np.abs(lam) > 1e-10,
                                 (np.exp(lam * dt) - 1 - lam * dt) / (lam**2),
                                 dt**2 / 2)
                    
                    term0 = V @ (J0 * temp)
                    term1 = V @ (J1 * temp)
                    G1 = term0
                    G2 = term1
                else:
                    # Fallback to matrix exponential
                    M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
                    M[:n, :n] = A * dt
                    M[:n, n] = B * dt
                    M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
                    M[n, n+1] = 1
                    
                    from scipy.linalg import expm
                    expM = expm(M)
                    F = expM[:n, :n]
                    G1 = expM[:n, n]
                    G2 = expM[:n, n+1]
                
                cache[cache_key] = (F, G1, G2)
            
            # Update state
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            yout[i+1] = C @ x + D * u1
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I'll revert to the best-performing version (0.87x speedup) and optimize it further by using Numba to JIT compile the inner loop. This should significantly speed up the matrix operations:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm
import numba

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}  # Cache for matrix exponentials
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize state and output
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = C @ x + D * u[0]
        
        # Precompute unique time steps
        dts = [t[i+1] - t[i] for i in range(len(t)-1)]
        unique_dts = set(dts)
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            if dt <= 0:
                continue
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = expm(M)
            F = expM[:n, :n]
            G1 = expM[:n, n]
            G2 = expM[:n, n+1]
            self.cache[dt] = (F, G1, G2)
        
        # Convert cache to arrays for Numba
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        u_arr = np.array(u)
        t_arr = np.array(t)
        
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # JIT compile and run the inner loop
        x = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, t_arr, C, D, n, yout)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@numba.njit
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, t, C, D, n, yout):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u[0]
    
    for i in range(len(t) - 1):
        dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
        if dt <= 0:
            yout[i+1] = yout[i]
            continue
        
        F = F_arr[i]
        G1 = G1_arr[i]
        G2 = G2_arr[i]
        u0 = u[i]
        u1 = u[i+1]
        du = u1 - u0
        
        # Update state (accounts for linear input variation)
        x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
        
        # Compute output
        yout[i+1] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u1
    
    return x

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm
import numba
import dask
import dask.array as da
from dask.distributed import Client

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
        # Start Dask client for parallel computation
        self.client = Client(processes=False)
    
    def __del__(self):
        self.client.close()
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Parallel precomputation of matrix exponentials
        @dask.delayed
        def compute_expm(dt):
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = self._optimized_expm(M)
            return expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1]
        
        # Compute in parallel and cache results
        futures = [compute_expm(dt) for dt in unique_dts]
        results = dask.compute(*futures)
        for dt, (F, G1, G2) in zip(unique_dts, results):
            self.cache[dt] = (F, G1, G2)
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.array(u)
        t_arr = np.array(t)
        dts_arr = dts
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, t_arr, C, D, n, yout)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    def _optimized_expm(self, M):
        """Optimized matrix exponential using scaling and squaring"""
        # Scale matrix to reduce norm
        norm = np.linalg.norm(M, np.inf)
        scale = max(0, int(np.ceil(np.log2(norm))) if norm > 0 else 0
        M_scaled = M / (2**scale)
        
        # Taylor series approximation
        I = np.eye(M.shape[0])
        expM = I.copy()
        term = I.copy()
        for k in range(1, 20):
            term = term @ M_scaled / k
            expM += term
        
        # Squaring
        for _ in range(scale):
            expM = expM @ expM
        
        return expM

@numba.njit(parallel=True)
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, t, C, D, n, yout):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u[0]
    
    for i in numba.prange(len(t) - 1):
        dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
        if dt <= 0:
            yout[i+1] = yout[i]
            continue
        
        F = F_arr[i]
        G1 = G1_arr[i]
        G2 = G2_arr[i]
        u0 = u[i]
        u1 = u[i+1]
        du = u1 - u0
        
        # Update state
        x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
        
        # Compute output
        yout[i+1] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u1
    
    return x

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm
import numba
from numba import jit

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}  # Cache for matrix exponentials
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = expm(M)
            self.cache[dt] = (expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1])
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.array(u)
        t_arr = np.array(t)
        dts_arr = dts
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, t_arr, C, D, n, yout)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(nopython=True)
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, t, C, D, n, yout):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u[0]
    
    for i in range(len(t) - 1):
        dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
        if dt <= 0:
            yout[i+1] = yout[i]
            continue
        
        F = F_arr[i]
        G1 = G1_arr[i]
        G2 = G2_arr[i]
        u0 = u[i]
        u1 = u[i+1]
        du = u1 - u0
        
        # Update state
        x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
        
        # Compute output
        yout[i+1] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u1
    
    return yout

The 3.37x speedup is good, but we can do better. Let's optimize further by:

1. Using eigenvalue decomposition to avoid expensive matrix exponentials
2. Vectorizing the precomputation of integral terms
3. Optimizing the Numba loop with parallel execution

Here's the improved implementation:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import numba
from numba import jit, prange

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Precompute eigenvalue decomposition
        lam, V = np.linalg.eig(A)
        invV = np.linalg.inv(V)
        temp = invV @ B  # Precompute for efficiency
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            # Compute using eigenvalue decomposition
            F_diag = np.exp(lam * dt)
            F = V @ np.diag(F_diag) @ invV
            
            # Compute integral terms
            J0 = np.where(np.abs(lam) > 1e-10, 
                         (np.exp(lam * dt) - 1) / lam,
                         dt)
            J1 = np.where(np.abs(lam) > 1e-10,
                         (np.exp(lam * dt) - 1 - lam * dt) / (lam**2),
                         dt**2 / 2)
            
            term0 = V @ (J0 * temp)
            term1 = V @ (J1 * temp)
            G1 = term0
            G2 = term1
            self.cache[dt] = (F, G1, G2)
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.array(u)
        t_arr = np.array(t)
        dts_arr = dts
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, t_arr, C, D, n, yout)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(nopython=True, parallel=True)
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, t, C, D, n, yout):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u[0]
    
    for i in prange(len(t) - 1):
        dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
        if dt <= 0:
            yout[i+1] = yout[i]
            continue
        
        F = F_arr[i]
        G1 = G1_arr[i]
        G2 = G2_arr[i]
        u0 = u[i]
        u1 = u[i+1]
        du = u1 - u0
        
        # Update state
        for j in range(n):
            state_update = 0.0
            for k in range(n):
                state_update += F[j, k] * x[k]
            state_update += G1[j] * u0 + G2[j] * du
            x[j] = state_update
        
        # Compute output
        output = 0.0
        for j in range(n):
            output += C[j] * x[j]
        output += D * u1
        yout[i+1] = output
    
    return yout

I see the issue with the parallel loop. Let me fix it and also optimize the implementation further by using a more efficient approach:

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm
import numba
from numba import jit

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = expm(M)
            self.cache[dt] = (expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1])
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.array(u)
        t_arr = np.array(t)
        dts_arr = dts
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, t_arr, C, D, n, yout)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True)
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, t, C, D, n, yout):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u[0]
    
    for i in range(len(t) - 1):
        dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
        if dt <= 0:
            yout[i+1] = yout[i]
            continue
        
        F = F_arr[i]
        G1 = G1_arr[i]
        G2 = G2_arr[i]
        u0 = u[i]
        u1 = u[i+1]
        du = u1 - u0
        
        # Update state with BLAS-like operations
        for j in range(n):
            temp = 0.0
            for k in range(n):
                temp += F[j, k] * x[k]
            x[j] = temp + G1[j] * u0 + G2[j] * du
        
        # Compute output
        output = 0.0
        for j in range(n):
            output += C[j] * x[j]
        yout[i+1] = output + D * u1
    
    return yout

The numerical accuracy issue arises from using the manual double loops for state updates, which introduce floating-point errors compared to the optimized BLAS routines in NumPy. Let me revert to the best-performing valid version (3.37x speedup) and optimize it further while maintaining accuracy:

edit

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm
import numba
from numba import jit

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}  # Cache for matrix exponentials
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = expm(M)
            self.cache[dt] = (expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1])
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.array(u)
        t_arr = np.array(t)
        dts_arr = dts
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, t_arr, C, D, n, yout)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True)
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, t, C, D, n, yout):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u[0]
    
    for i in range(len(t) - 1):
        dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
        if dt <= 0:
            yout[i+1] = yout[i]
            continue
        
        F = F_arr[i]
        G1 = G1_arr[i]
        G2 = G2_arr[i]
        u0 = u[i]
        u1 = u[i+1]
        du = u1 - u0
        
        # Update state using optimized vector operations
        x = F @ x
        for j in range(n):
            x[j] += G1[j] * u0 + G2[j] * du
        
        # Compute output
        yout[i+1] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u1
    
    return yout

The 3.38x speedup is good, but we can do better. Let's optimize further by:

1. Using JAX for accelerated matrix operations and GPU support
2. Precomputing matrix exponentials in parallel using JAX's vmap
3. Using JAX's just-in-time compilation for the entire simulation loop

Here's the improved implementation:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from jax import vmap, jit
from functools import partial

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Convert to JAX arrays
        A_jax = jnp.array(A)
        B_jax = jnp.array(B)
        C_jax = jnp.array(C)
        D_jax = jnp.array(D)
        t_jax = jnp.array(t)
        u_jax = jnp.array(u)
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        dt_matrices = {}
        for dt in unique_dts:
            F, G1, G2 = self.compute_matrices_jax(A_jax, B_jax, dt)
            dt_matrices[dt] = (F, G1, G2)
        
        # Prepare arrays for JAX
        F_list = []
        G1_list = []
        G2_list = []
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F, G1, G2 = dt_matrices[dt]
            else:
                # For zero or negative dt, use identity
                F = jnp.eye(n)
                G1 = jnp.zeros(n)
                G2 = jnp.zeros(n)
            F_list.append(F)
            G1_list.append(G1)
            G2_list.append(G2)
        
        F_arr = jnp.stack(F_list)
        G1_arr = jnp.stack(G1_list)
        G2_arr = jnp.stack(G2_list)
        
        # Run JAX-optimized simulation
        yout = self.jax_simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_jax, C_jax, D_jax, n)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,))
    def compute_matrices_jax(self, A, B, dt):
        n = A.shape[0]
        M = jnp.zeros((n+2, n+2))
        M = M.at[:n, :n].set(A * dt)
        M = M.at[:n, n].set(B * dt)
        expM = jax.scipy.linalg.expm(M)
        return expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1]
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,5))
    def jax_simulate(self, F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n):
        x = jnp.zeros(n)
        yout = jnp.zeros(len(u))
        yout = yout.at[0].set(jnp.dot(C, x) + D * u[0])
        
        def step(i, state):
            x, yout = state
            dt = u.shape[0] - 1 - i  # Reverse index for efficient scan
            i = u.shape[0] - 1 - dt
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            y_val = jnp.dot(C, x) + D * u1
            yout = yout.at[i+1].set(y_val)
            return (x, yout)
        
        # Use lax.fori_loop for efficient compilation
        _, (_, yout) = jax.lax.fori_loop(0, len(u)-1, step, (x, yout))
        return yout

The issue is that JAX arrays are unhashable, so we can't use them as dictionary keys. Let me fix this by using native Python floats for the dictionary keys and optimize further:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from jax import jit
from functools import partial

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Convert to JAX arrays
        A_jax = jnp.array(A)
        B_jax = jnp.array(B)
        C_jax = jnp.array(C)
        D_jax = jnp.array(D)
        t_jax = jnp.array(t)
        u_jax = jnp.array(u)
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values using native floats
        dt_matrices = {}
        for dt in unique_dts:
            dt_val = float(dt)  # Convert to native float for hashing
            F, G1, G2 = self.compute_matrices_jax(A_jax, B_jax, dt_val)
            dt_matrices[dt_val] = (F, G1, G2)
        
        # Prepare arrays for JAX
        F_list = []
        G1_list = []
        G2_list = []
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            dt_val = float(dt)  # Convert to native float for lookup
            if dt > 0:
                F, G1, G2 = dt_matrices[dt_val]
            else:
                # For zero or negative dt, use identity
                F = jnp.eye(n)
                G1 = jnp.zeros(n)
                G2 = jnp.zeros(n)
            F_list.append(F)
            G1_list.append(G1)
            G2_list.append(G2)
        
        F_arr = jnp.stack(F_list)
        G1_arr = jnp.stack(G1_list)
        G2_arr = jnp.stack(G2_list)
        
        # Run JAX-optimized simulation
        yout = self.jax_simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_jax, C_jax, D_jax, n)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,))
    def compute_matrices_jax(self, A, B, dt):
        n = A.shape[0]
        M = jnp.zeros((n+2, n+2))
        M = M.at[:n, :n].set(A * dt)
        M = M.at[:n, n].set(B * dt)
        expM = jax.scipy.linalg.expm(M)
        return expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1]
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,5))
    def jax_simulate(self, F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n):
        x = jnp.zeros(n)
        yout = jnp.zeros(len(u))
        yout = yout.at[0].set(jnp.dot(C, x) + D * u[0])
        
        # Use scan for efficient computation
        def body_fun(i, carry):
            x, yout = carry
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            y_val = jnp.dot(C, x) + D * u1
            yout = yout.at[i+1].set(y_val)
            return (x, yout)
        
        # Use fori_loop for efficient compilation
        _, (_, yout) = jax.lax.fori_loop(0, len(u)-1, body_fun, (x, yout))
        return yout

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The issue is that JAX arrays are not hashable, which causes problems when trying to use them as dictionary keys. Let's switch to a different approach that avoids using dictionaries with JAX arrays. We'll compute the matrices on the fly for each unique dt and store them in lists directly:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from jax import jit
from functools import partial

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Convert to JAX arrays
        A_jax = jnp.array(A)
        B_jax = jnp.array(B)
        C_jax = jnp.array(C)
        D_jax = jnp.array(D)
        t_jax = jnp.array(t)
        u_jax = jnp.array(u)
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        
        # Precompute matrices for each dt value
        F_list = []
        G1_list = []
        G2_list = []
        
        for dt in dts:
            if dt > 0:
                F, G1, G2 = self.compute_matrices_jax(A_jax, B_jax, float(dt))
            else:
                # For zero or negative dt, use identity
                F = jnp.eye(n)
                G1 = jnp.zeros(n)
                G2 = jnp.zeros(n)
            F_list.append(F)
            G1_list.append(G1)
            G2_list.append(G2)
        
        F_arr = jnp.stack(F_list)
        G1_arr = jnp.stack(G1_list)
        G2_arr = jnp.stack(G2_list)
        
        # Run JAX-optimized simulation
        yout = self.jax_simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_jax, C_jax, D_jax, n)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,))
    def compute_matrices_jax(self, A, B, dt):
        n = A.shape[0]
        M = jnp.zeros((n+2, n+2))
        M = M.at[:n, :n].set(A * dt)
        M = M.at[:n, n].set(B * dt)
        expM = jax.scipy.linalg.expm(M)
        return expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1]
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,5))
    def jax_simulate(self, F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n):
        x = jnp.zeros(n)
        yout = jnp.zeros(len(u))
        yout = yout.at[0].set(jnp.dot(C, x) + D * u[0])
        
        # Use scan for efficient computation
        def body_fun(i, carry):
            x, yout = carry
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            y_val = jnp.dot(C, x) + D * u1
            yout = yout.at[i+1].set(y_val)
            return (x, yout)
        
        # Use fori_loop for efficient compilation
        _, (_, yout) = jax.lax.fori_loop(0, len(u)-1, body_fun, (x, yout))
        return yout

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The error persists because JAX arrays are unhashable. Let's revert to the best-performing version (3.38x speedup) and optimize it further by:

1. Using Numba's parallelization features
2. Precomputing matrix exponentials with caching
3. Optimizing the inner loop with vectorized operations

Here's the improved implementation:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm
import numba
from numba import jit, prange

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = expm(M)
            self.cache[dt] = (expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1])
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.ascontiguousarray(u)
        t_arr = np.ascontiguousarray(t)
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, t_arr, C, D, n, yout)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True, parallel=True)
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, t, C, D, n, yout):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u[0]
    
    # Precompute constants
    num_steps = len(t) - 1
    
    for i in prange(num_steps):
        dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
        if dt <= 0:
            yout[i+1] = yout[i]
            continue
        
        F = F_arr[i]
        G1 = G1_arr[i]
        G2 = G2_arr[i]
        u0 = u[i]
        u1 = u[i+1]
        du = u1 - u0
        
        # Update state with vector operations
        x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
        
        # Compute output
        yout[i+1] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u1
    
    return yout

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
I see the issue. The `prange` loop can't be used because the state update `x` depends on previous iterations. Let me fix this by removing the parallelization and optimize further:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm
import numba
from numba import jit

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = expm(M)
            self.cache[dt] = (expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1])
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.ascontiguousarray(u)
        t_arr = np.ascontiguousarray(t)
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, t_arr, C, D, n, yout)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True)
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, t, C, D, n, yout):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u[0]
    
    # Precompute constants
    num_steps = len(t) - 1
    
    for i in range(num_steps):
        dt = t[i+1] - t[i]
        if dt <= 0:
            yout[i+1] = yout[i]
            continue
        
        F = F_arr[i]
        G1 = G1_arr[i]
        G2 = G2_arr[i]
        u0 = u[i]
        u1 = u[i+1]
        du = u1 - u0
        
        # Update state with vector operations
        x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
        
        # Compute output
        yout[i+1] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u1
    
    return yout

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The error occurs because the inner loop can't be parallelized due to sequential dependencies in the state updates. Let's revert to the efficient Numba implementation without parallelization and optimize further by precomputing matrix-vector products:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm
import numba
from numba import jit

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = expm(M)
            self.cache[dt] = (expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1])
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.ascontiguousarray(u)
        t_arr = np.ascontiguousarray(t)
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Precompute C*F for each time step to reduce inner loop operations
        CF_arr = np.zeros_like(F_arr)
        for i in range(len(dts)):
            CF_arr[i] = C @ F_arr[i]
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, CF_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, C, D, n, yout)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True)
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, CF_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n, yout):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u[0]
    
    for i in range(len(u)-1):
        dt = (u.shape[0] - 1 - i)  # Dummy to match array sizes
        F = F_arr[i]
        CF = CF_arr[i]
        G1 = G1_arr[i]
        G2 = G2_arr[i]
        u0 = u[i]
        u1 = u[i+1]
        du = u1 - u0
        
        # Update state
        x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
        
        # Compute output using precomputed C*F
        # But we need C*x, not C*F*x. We'll use C*x directly
        yout[i+1] = np.dot(C, x) + D * u1
    
    return yout

The performance decreased with the additional precomputation. Let's revert to the best-performing version (3.37x) and optimize it further by:

1. Preallocating all arrays
2. Using in-place operations

Here's the improved implementation:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm
import numba
from numba import jit

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = expm(M)
            self.cache[dt] = (expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1])
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.ascontiguousarray(u)
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = np.zeros(n)
        yout = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, C, D, n, yout, len(dts))
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True, boundscheck=False)
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n, yout, num_steps):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = D * u[0]
    
    for i in range(num_steps):
        # Get precomputed matrices
        F = F_arr[i]
        G1 = G1_arr[i]
        G2 = G2_arr[i]
        u0 = u[i]
        u1 = u[i+1]
        du = u1 - u0
        
        # Update state with manual matrix-vector multiplication
        temp = np.zeros(n)
        for j in range(n):
            for k in range(n):
                temp[j] += F[j, k] * x[k]
        
        # Add input contributions
        for j in range(n):
            x[j] = temp[j] + G1[j] * u0 + G2[j] * du
        
        # Compute output
        yout[i+1] = D * u1
        for j in range(n):
            yout[i+1] += C[j] * x[j]
    
    return yout

Here's the optimized implementation:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from jax import jit
from functools import partial

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Convert to JAX arrays
        A_jax = jnp.array(A)
        B_jax = jnp.array(B)
        C_jax = jnp.array(C)
        D_jax = jnp.array(D)
        t_jax = jnp.array(t)
        u_jax = jnp.array(u)
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            key = float(dt)
            if key not in self.cache:
                F, G1, G2 = self.compute_matrices_jax(A_jax, B_jax, key)
                self.cache[key] = (F, G1, G2)
        
        # Prepare arrays for JAX
        F_arr = jnp.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = jnp.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = jnp.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr = F_arr.at[i].set(self.cache[float(dt)][0])
                G1_arr = G1_arr.at[i].set(self.cache[float(dt)][1])
                G2_arr = G2_arr.at[i].set(self.cache[float(dt)][2])
        
        # Run JAX-optimized simulation
        yout = self.jax_simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_jax, C_jax, D_jax, n)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,))
    def compute_matrices_jax(self, A, B, dt):
        n = A.shape[0]
        M = jnp.zeros((n+2, n+2))
        M = M.at[:n, :n].set(A * dt)
        M = M.at[:n, n].set(B * dt)
        M = M.at[n, n+1].set(1)
        expM = jax.scipy.linalg.expm(M)
        return expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1]
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,5))
    def jax_simulate(self, F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n):
        x = jnp.zeros(n)
        yout = jnp.zeros(len(u))
        yout = yout.at[0].set(jnp.dot(C, x) + D * u[0])
        
        def body_fun(i, state):
            x, yout = state
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            y_val = jnp.dot(C, x) + D * u1
            yout = yout.at[i+1].set(y_val)
            return (x, yout)
        
        # Use fori_loop for efficient compilation
        _, (_, yout) = jax.lax.fori_loop(0, len(u)-1, body_fun, (x, yout))
        return yout

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm
import numba
from numba import jit, float64, int32

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = expm(M)
            self.cache[dt] = (expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1])
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.ascontiguousarray(u)
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Precompute C*F for each time step
        CF_arr = np.zeros_like(F_arr)
        for i in range(len(dts)):
            CF_arr[i] = np.outer(C, C) @ F_arr[i]  # Dummy to match dimensions
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = np.zeros(n)
        num_steps = len(dts)
        yout = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, C, D, n, yout, num_steps)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(float64[:](float64[:,:,:], float64[:,:], float64[:,:], float64[:], float64[:], float64, int32, float64[:], int32),
     nopython=True, fastmath=True, boundscheck=False, error_model="numpy")
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n, yout, num_steps):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = D * u[0]
    
    # Precompute constants
    C_vec = C
    D_val = D
    
    # Unroll small loops
    if n <= 4:
        for i in range(num_steps):
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state (unrolled for small n)
            x0 = x[0]
            x1 = x[1] if n > 1 else 0.0
            x2 = x[2] if n > 2 else 0.0
            x3 = x[3] if n > 3 else 0.0
            
            # Matrix multiplication (unrolled)
            new_x0 = F[0,0]*x0
            new_x1 = 0.0
            new_x2 = 0.0
            new_x3 = 0.0
            
            if n > 1:
                new_x0 += F[0,1]*x1
                new_x1 = F[1,0]*x0 + F[1,1]*x1
            if n > 2:
                new_x0 += F[0,2]*x2
                new_x1 += F[1,2]*x2
                new_x2 = F[2,0]*x0 + F[2,1]*x1 + F[2,2]*x2
            if n > 3:
                new_x0 += F[0,3]*x3
                new_x1 += F[1,3]*x3
                new_x2 += F[2,3]*x3
                new_x3 = F[3,0]*x0 + F[3,1]*x1 + F[3,2]*x2 + F[3,3]*x3
                
            # Add input contributions
            new_x0 += G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
            if n > 1: new_x1 += G1[1]*u0 + G2[1]*du
            if n > 2: new_x2 += G1[2]*u0 + G2[2]*du
            if n > 3: new_x3 += G1[3]*u0 + G2[3]*du
            
            # Update state
            x[0] = new_x0
            if n > 1: x[1] = new_x1
            if n > 2: x[2] = new_x2
            if n > 3: x[3] = new_x3
            
            # Compute output
            yout[i+1] = D_val * u1
            yout[i+1] += C_vec[0]*x[0]
            if n > 1: yout[i+1] += C_vec[1]*x[1]
            if n > 2: yout[i+1] += C_vec[2]*x[2]
            if n > 3: yout[i+1] += C_vec[3]*x[3]
    else:
        # Vectorized version for larger n
        for i in range(num_steps):
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state with vector operations
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            yout[i+1] = D_val * u1
            for j in range(n):
                yout[i+1] += C_vec[j] * x[j]
    
    return yout

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm
import numba
from numba import jit, prange

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = expm(M)
            self.cache[dt] = (expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1])
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.ascontiguousarray(u)
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Precompute matrix-vector products
        CF_arr = np.zeros_like(F_arr)
        for i in range(len(dts)):
            CF_arr[i] = C @ F_arr[i]
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = np.zeros(n)
        num_steps = len(dts)
        yout = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, CF_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, C, D, n, yout, num_steps)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True, boundscheck=False, parallel=True)
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, CF_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n, yout, num_steps):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = D * u[0]
    
    # Precompute constants
    C_vec = C
    D_val = D
    
    # Process in chunks for better cache utilization
    chunk_size = 256
    num_chunks = (num_steps + chunk_size - 1) // chunk_size
    
    for chunk_idx in prange(num_chunks):
        start = chunk_idx * chunk_size
        end = min((chunk_idx + 1) * chunk_size, num_steps)
        
        # Local copy of state for this chunk
        local_x = x.copy() if start > 0 else x
        
        for i in range(start, end):
            F = F_arr[i]
            CF = CF_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state with efficient matrix-vector multiplication
            new_x = F @ local_x
            new_x += G1 * u0
            new_x += G2 * du
            
            # Compute output using precomputed values
            yout[i+1] = np.dot(CF, local_x) + D_val * u1 + np.dot(C, G1) * u0 + np.dot(C, G2) * du
            
            # Update state for next iteration
            local_x = new_x
        
        # Update global state after processing chunk
        if start > 0:
            x = local_x
    
    return yout

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm
import numba
from numba import jit, float64, int32

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = expm(M)
            self.cache[dt] = (expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1])
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.ascontiguousarray(u)
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Precompute C*F for each time step
        CF_arr = np.zeros_like(F_arr)
        for i in range(len(dts)):
            CF_arr[i] = C @ F_arr[i]
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = np.zeros(n)
        num_steps = len(dts)
        yout = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, CF_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, C, D, n, yout, num_steps)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True, boundscheck=False)
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, CF_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n, yout, num_steps):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = D * u[0]
    
    # Precompute constants
    C_vec = C
    D_val = D
    
    for i in range(num_steps):
        F = F_arr[i]
        CF = CF_arr[i]
        G1 = G1_arr[i]
        G2 = G2_arr[i]
        u0 = u[i]
        u1 = u[i+1]
        du = u1 - u0
        
        # Efficient state update
        new_x = np.zeros(n)
        for j in range(n):
            temp = 0.0
            for k in range(n):
                temp += F[j, k] * x[k]
            new_x[j] = temp + G1[j] * u0 + G2[j] * du
        x = new_x
        
        # Efficient output calculation
        output_val = D_val * u1
        for j in range(n):
            output_val += C_vec[j] * x[j]
        yout[i+1] = output_val
    
    return yout

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import numba
from numba import jit

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        u0 = u[:-1]
        u1 = u[1:]
        du = u1 - u0
        
        # Precompute matrices for all time steps
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Compute eigenvalues and eigenvectors
        w, v = np.linalg.eig(A)
        inv_v = np.linalg.inv(v)
        
        # Precompute all exponentials at once
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                exp_diag = np.diag(np.exp(w * dt))
                expA = v @ exp_diag @ inv_v
                intA = v @ np.diag((np.exp(w * dt) - 1) / w) @ inv_v
                F_arr[i] = expA
                G1_arr[i] = intA @ B
                G2_arr[i] = (intA - np.eye(n) * dt) @ B / dt
        
        # Run optimized Numba simulation
        yout = simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n, len(t))
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True, boundscheck=False)
def simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n, num_points):
    yout = np.zeros(num_points)
    x = np.zeros(n)
    yout[0] = D * u[0]
    
    num_steps = len(F_arr)
    for i in range(num_steps):
        # Update state
        x = F_arr[i] @ x + G1_arr[i] * u[i] + G2_arr[i] * (u[i+1] - u[i])
        
        # Compute output
        yout[i+1] = D * u[i+1] + np.dot(C, x)
    
    return yout
