import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
from scipy.linalg import expm
import numba
from numba import jit, float64, int32

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values in a vectorized way
        for dt in unique_dts:
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = expm(M)
            self.cache[dt] = (expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1])
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.ascontiguousarray(u)
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = np.zeros(n)
        num_steps = len(dts)
        yout = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, C, D, n, yout, num_steps)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True, boundscheck=False)
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n, yout, num_steps):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    D_val = D
    C_vec = C
    
    # Handle small systems with unrolled loops
    if n <= 4:
        for i in range(num_steps):
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state (unrolled for n<=4)
            new_x = np.zeros(n)
            if n >= 1:
                new_x[0] = F[0,0]*x[0]
                if n >= 2: new_x[0] += F[0,1]*x[1]
                if n >= 3: new_x[0] += F[0,2]*x[2]
                if n >= 4: new_x[0] += F[0,3]*x[3]
                new_x[0] += G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
                
            if n >= 2:
                new_x[1] = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1]
                if n >= 3: new_x[1] += F[1,2]*x[2]
                if n >= 4: new_x[1] += F[1,3]*x[3]
                new_x[1] += G1[1]*u0 + G2[1]*du
                
            if n >= 3:
                new_x[2] = F[2,0]*x[0] + F[2,1]*x[1] + F[2,2]*x[2]
                if n >= 4: new_x[2] += F[2,3]*x[3]
                new_x[2] += G1[2]*u0 + G2[2]*du
                
            if n >= 4:
                new_x[3] = F[3,0]*x[0] + F[3,1]*x[1] + F[3,2]*x[2] + F[3,3]*x[3]
                new_x[3] += G1[3]*u0 + G2[3]*du
            
            x = new_x
            
            # Compute output
            output_val = D_val * u1
            if n >= 1: output_val += C_vec[0]*x[0]
            if n >= 2: output_val += C_vec[1]*x[1]
            if n >= 3: output_val += C_vec[2]*x[2]
            if n >= 4: output_val += C_vec[3]*x[3]
            yout[i+1] = output_val
    else:
        # For larger systems, use optimized BLAS-style operations
        for i in range(num_steps):
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Efficient state update
            new_x = np.zeros(n)
            for j in range(n):
                temp = 0.0
                for k in range(n):
                    temp += F[j, k] * x[k]
                new_x[j] = temp + G1[j] * u0 + G2[j] * du
            x = new_x
            
            # Efficient output calculation
            output_val = D_val * u1
            for j in range(n):
                output_val += C_vec[j] * x[j]
            yout[i+1] = output_val
    
    return yout

The 3.59x speedup is good progress, but we can still improve performance. Let's optimize further by:

1. Using JAX for GPU acceleration
2. Implementing a custom matrix exponential using Taylor series
3. Precomputing all exponentials in parallel
4. Using JIT compilation for the entire computation

Here's the optimized implementation:

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from jax import jit, vmap
from functools import partial

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Convert to JAX arrays
        A = jnp.array(A)
        B = jnp.array(B)
        C = jnp.array(C)
        D = jnp.array(D)
        u = jnp.array(u)
        t = jnp.array(t)
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = jnp.diff(t)
        
        # Precompute all exponentials at once using JAX
        F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr = self.precompute_exponentials(A, B, dts)
        
        # Run optimized JAX simulation
        yout = self.simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,))
    def precompute_exponentials(self, A, B, dts):
        # Vectorized matrix exponential using Taylor series
        def compute_matrices(dt):
            # Use Taylor series for matrix exponential
            I = jnp.eye(A.shape[0])
            M = I
            expA = I
            fact = 1.0
            
            # 8-term Taylor series approximation
            for k in range(1, 8):
                fact *= k
                M = M @ (A * dt)
                expA += M / fact
            
            # Compute integral terms
            intA = jnp.linalg.inv(A) @ (expA - I) if jnp.linalg.det(A) != 0 else I * dt
            G1 = intA @ B
            G2 = (intA - I * dt) @ B / dt
            return expA, G1, G2
        
        # Vectorize over all time steps
        return vmap(compute_matrices)(dts)
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,5))
    def simulate(self, F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n):
        yout = jnp.zeros(len(u))
        yout = yout.at[0].set(D * u[0])
        x = jnp.zeros(n)
        
        def step(i, state):
            x, yout = state
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            output_val = D * u1 + jnp.dot(C, x)
            yout = yout.at[i+1].set(output_val)
            return (x, yout)
        
        # Process all time steps
        _, yout = jax.lax.fori_loop(0, len(F_arr), step, (x, yout))
        return yout

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The error occurs because JAX doesn't allow Python conditionals with traced values. Let's fix this by:

1. Using JAX's control flow primitives
2. Implementing a safer matrix exponential
3. Adding numerical stability checks

Here's the corrected implementation:

edit
file: solver.py
lines: 0-1000
---
import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from jax import jit, vmap, lax
from functools import partial

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Convert to JAX arrays
        A = jnp.array(A)
        B = jnp.array(B)
        C = jnp.array(C)
        D = jnp.array(D)
        u = jnp.array(u)
        t = jnp.array(t)
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = jnp.diff(t)
        
        # Precompute all exponentials at once using JAX
        F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr = self.precompute_exponentials(A, B, dts)
        
        # Run optimized JAX simulation
        yout = self.simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,))
    def precompute_exponentials(self, A, B, dts):
        # Vectorized matrix exponential using Taylor series
        def compute_matrices(dt):
            # Use Taylor series for matrix exponential
            I = jnp.eye(A.shape[0])
            M = I
            expA = I
            fact = 1.0
            
            # 8-term Taylor series approximation
            for k in range(1, 8):
                fact *= k
                M = M @ (A * dt)
                expA += M / fact
            
            # Compute integral terms safely
            cond = jnp.linalg.cond(A)
            intA = lax.cond(
                cond < 1e10,
                lambda: jnp.linalg.solve(A, expA - I),
                lambda: I * dt
            )
            G1 = intA @ B
            G2 = (intA - I * dt) @ B / dt
            return expA, G1, G2
        
        # Vectorize over all time steps
        return vmap(compute_matrices)(dts)
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,5))
    def simulate(self, F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n):
        yout = jnp.zeros(len(u))
        yout = yout.at[0].set(D * u[0])
        x = jnp.zeros(n)
        
        # Define a single step function
        def step(carry, i):
            x, yout = carry
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            output_val = D * u1 + jnp.dot(C, x)
            yout = yout.at[i+1].set(output_val)
            return (x, yout), None
        
        # Process all time steps
        (x, yout), _ = lax.scan(step, (x, yout), jnp.arange(len(F_arr)))
        return yout

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The error occurs because JAX arrays are unhashable and can't be used in Python conditionals. Let's fix this by:

1. Removing the cache since it's not being used
2. Using JAX's control flow primitives properly
3. Simplifying the matrix exponential computation

Here's the corrected implementation:

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from jax import jit, vmap, lax
from functools import partial

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Convert to JAX arrays
        A = jnp.array(A)
        B = jnp.array(B)
        C = jnp.array(C)
        D = jnp.array(D)
        u = jnp.array(u)
        t = jnp.array(t)
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = jnp.diff(t)
        
        # Precompute all exponentials at once using JAX
        F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr = self.precompute_exponentials(A, B, dts)
        
        # Run optimized JAX simulation
        yout = self.simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,))
    def precompute_exponentials(self, A, B, dts):
        # Vectorized matrix exponential using Taylor series
        def compute_matrices(dt):
            # Use Taylor series for matrix exponential
            I = jnp.eye(A.shape[0])
            M = I
            expA = I
            fact = 1.0
            
            # 8-term Taylor series approximation
            for k in range(1, 8):
                fact *= k
                M = M @ (A * dt)
                expA += M / fact
            
            # Compute integral terms safely
            intA = jnp.linalg.solve(A, expA - I) if jnp.linalg.det(A) > 1e-8 else I * dt
            G1 = intA @ B
            G2 = (intA - I * dt) @ B / dt
            return expA, G1, G2
        
        # Vectorize over all time steps
        return vmap(compute_matrices)(dts)
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,5))
    def simulate(self, F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n):
        yout = jnp.zeros(len(u))
        yout = yout.at[0].set(D * u[0])
        x = jnp.zeros(n)
        
        # Define a single step function
        def step(i, state):
            x, yout = state
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            output_val = D * u1 + jnp.dot(C, x)
            yout = yout.at[i+1].set(output_val)
            return (x, yout)
        
        # Process all time steps
        _, yout = lax.fori_loop(0, len(F_arr), step, (x, yout))
        return yout

The issue is still with the Python conditional in the JIT-compiled function. Let's fix it by using JAX's `lax.cond` for safe conditional branching:

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import jax
import jax.numpy as jnp
from jax import jit, vmap, lax
from functools import partial

class Solver:
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Convert to JAX arrays
        A = jnp.array(A)
        B = jnp.array(B)
        C = jnp.array(C)
        D = jnp.array(D)
        u = jnp.array(u)
        t = jnp.array(t)
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = jnp.diff(t)
        
        # Precompute all exponentials at once using JAX
        F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr = self.precompute_exponentials(A, B, dts)
        
        # Run optimized JAX simulation
        yout = self.simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,))
    def precompute_exponentials(self, A, B, dts):
        # Vectorized matrix exponential using Taylor series
        def compute_matrices(dt):
            # Use Taylor series for matrix exponential
            I = jnp.eye(A.shape[0])
            M = I
            expA = I
            fact = 1.0
            
            # 8-term Taylor series approximation
            for k in range(1, 8):
                fact *= k
                M = M @ (A * dt)
                expA += M / fact
            
            # Compute integral terms safely using JAX control flow
            intA = lax.cond(
                jnp.linalg.det(A) > 1e-8,
                lambda: jnp.linalg.solve(A, expA - I),
                lambda: I * dt
            )
            G1 = intA @ B
            G2 = (intA - I * dt) @ B / dt
            return expA, G1, G2
        
        # Vectorize over all time steps
        return vmap(compute_matrices)(dts)
    
    @partial(jit, static_argnums=(0,5))
    def simulate(self, F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n):
        yout = jnp.zeros(len(u))
        yout = yout.at[0].set(D * u[0])
        x = jnp.zeros(n)
        
        # Define a single step function
        def step(i, state):
            x, yout = state
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state
            x = F @ x + G1 * u0 + G2 * du
            
            # Compute output
            output_val = D * u1 + jnp.dot(C, x)
            yout = yout.at[i+1].set(output_val)
            return (x, yout)
        
        # Process all time steps
        _, yout = lax.fori_loop(0, len(F_arr), step, (x, yout))
        return yout

The JAX implementation is causing too many issues with unhashable arrays and tracer errors. Let's revert to the best-performing Numba implementation (3.59x speedup) and optimize it further by:

1. Using a custom matrix exponential function with Taylor series approximation
2. Optimizing the state update with loop unrolling for small systems

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import numba
from numba import jit, float64

@jit(nopython=True)
def taylor_expm(M, max_terms=15):
    n = M.shape[0]
    expM = np.eye(n)
    term = np.eye(n)
    for k in range(1, max_terms+1):
        term = term @ M / k
        expM += term
    return expM

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
        
        # Precompute matrices for all unique dt values
        for dt in unique_dts:
            M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
            M[:n, :n] = A * dt
            M[:n, n] = B * dt
            M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
            M[n, n+1] = 1
            expM = taylor_expm(M)
            self.cache[dt] = (expM[:n, :n], expM[:n, n], expM[:n, n+1])
        
        # Prepare arrays for Numba
        u_arr = np.ascontiguousarray(u)
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        # Map time steps to precomputed matrices
        for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
            if dt > 0:
                F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
        
        # Run optimized Numba loop
        x = np.zeros(n)
        num_steps = len(dts)
        yout = numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, C, D, n, yout, num_steps)
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True, boundscheck=False)
def numba_jit_loop(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n, yout, num_steps):
    x = np.zeros(n)
    D_val = D
    C_vec = C
    
    # Small system optimization
    if n == 1:
        for i in range(num_steps):
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state
            x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
            x[0] = x0
            
            # Compute output
            yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0
    elif n == 2:
        for i in range(num_steps):
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state
            x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
            x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + G1[1]*u0 + G2[1]*du
            x[0], x[1] = x0, x1
            
            # Compute output
            yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1
    elif n == 3:
        for i in range(num_steps):
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state
            x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + F[0,2]*x[2] + G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
            x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + F[1,2]*x[2] + G1[1]*u0 + G2[1]*du
            x2 = F[2,0]*x[0] + F[2,1]*x[1] + F[2,2]*x[2] + G1[2]*u0 + G2[2]*du
            x[0], x[1], x[2] = x0, x1, x2
            
            # Compute output
            yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1 + C_vec[2]*x2
    elif n == 4:
        for i in range(num_steps):
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state
            x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + F[0,2]*x[2] + F[0,3]*x[3] + G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
            x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + F[1,2]*x[2] + F[1,3]*x[3] + G1[1]*u0 + G2[1]*du
            x2 = F[2,0]*x[0] + F[2,1]*x[1] + F[2,2]*x[2] + F[2,3]*x[3] + G1[2]*u0 + G2[2]*du
            x3 = F[3,0]*x[0] + F[3,1]*x[1] + F[3,2]*x[2] + F[3,3]*x[3] + G1[3]*u0 + G2[3]*du
            x[0], x[1], x[2], x[3] = x0, x1, x2, x3
            
            # Compute output
            yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1 + C_vec[2]*x2 + C_vec[3]*x3
    else:
        # For larger systems
        for i in range(num_steps):
            F = F_arr[i]
            G1 = G1_arr[i]
            G2 = G2_arr[i]
            u0 = u[i]
            u1 = u[i+1]
            du = u1 - u0
            
            # Update state
            new_x = np.zeros(n)
            for j in range(n):
                temp = 0.0
                for k in range(n):
                    temp += F[j, k] * x[k]
                new_x[j] = temp + G1[j] * u0 + G2[j] * du
            x = new_x
            
            # Compute output
            output_val = D_val * u1
            for j in range(n):
                output_val += C_vec[j] * x[j]
            yout[i+1] = output_val
    
    return yout

The previous implementations had issues with numerical accuracy and performance. I'll now implement a highly optimized solution using the following techniques:
1. Precompute state transition matrices using matrix exponentials
2. Use Numba for JIT compilation of the simulation loop
3. Specialize the inner loop for small system orders (1-4) for maximum speed
4. Efficiently handle systems with constant time steps

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import numba
from numba import jit, float64

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True)
def taylor_expm(M, max_terms=15):
    """Compute matrix exponential using Taylor series approximation."""
    n = M.shape[0]
    expM = np.eye(n)
    term = np.eye(n)
    for k in range(1, max_terms+1):
        term = term @ M / k
        expM += term
    return expM

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        constant_dt = np.all(np.abs(dts - dts[0]) < 1e-10)
        
        # Precompute matrices
        if constant_dt:
            # Single dt for all steps
            dt = dts[0]
            if dt > 0:
                if dt not in self.cache:
                    M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
                    M[:n, :n] = A * dt
                    M[:n, n] = B * dt
                    expM = taylor_expm(M)
                    F = expM[:n, :n]
                    G1 = expM[:n, n]
                    self.cache[dt] = (F, G1)
                F_arr, G1_arr = self.cache[dt]
                F_arr = np.tile(F_arr, (len(dts), 1, 1))
                G1_arr = np.tile(G1_arr, (len(dts), 1))
            else:
                F_arr = np.tile(np.eye(n), (len(dts), 1, 1))
                G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        else:
            # Variable time steps
            unique_dts = np.unique(dts[dts > 0])
            F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
            G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
            
            # Precompute for unique dt values
            for dt in unique_dts:
                if dt not in self.cache:
                    M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
                    M[:n, :n] = A * dt
                    M[:n, n] = B * dt
                    expM = taylor_expm(M)
                    F = expM[:n, :n]
                    G1 = expM[:n, n]
                    self.cache[dt] = (F, G1)
            
            # Map to all time steps
            for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
                if dt > 0:
                    F_arr[i], G1_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
                else:
                    F_arr[i] = np.eye(n)
        
        # Run optimized simulation
        x = np.zeros(n)
        u_arr = np.asarray(u)
        yout = self.numba_simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, u_arr, C, D, n, yout, len(dts))
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    @staticmethod
    @jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True, boundscheck=False)
    def numba_simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, u, C, D, n, yout, num_steps):
        x = np.zeros(n)
        D_val = D
        C_vec = C
        
        # Specialized loops for common system orders
        if n == 1:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                
                # State update
                x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + G1[0]*u0
                x[0] = x0
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0
        elif n == 2:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                
                # State update
                x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + G1[0]*u0
                x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + G1[1]*u0
                x[0], x[1] = x0, x1
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1
        elif n == 3:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                
                # State update
                x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + F[0,2]*x[2] + G1[0]*u0
                x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + F[1,2]*x[2] + G1[1]*u0
                x2 = F[2,0]*x[0] + F[2,1]*x[1] + F[2,2]*x[2] + G1[2]*u0
                x[0], x[1], x[2] = x0, x1, x2
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1 + C_vec[2]*x2
        elif n == 4:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                
                # State update
                x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + F[0,2]*x[2] + F[0,3]*x[3] + G1[0]*u0
                x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + F[1,2]*x[2] + F[1,3]*x[3] + G1[1]*u0
                x2 = F[2,0]*x[0] + F[2,1]*x[1] + F[2,2]*x[2] + F[2,3]*x[3] + G1[2]*u0
                x3 = F[3,0]*x[0] + F[3,1]*x[1] + F[3,2]*x[2] + F[3,3]*x[3] + G1[3]*u0
                x[0], x[1], x[2], x[3] = x0, x1, x2, x3
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1 + C_vec[2]*x2 + C_vec[3]*x3
        else:
            # General case for higher-order systems
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                
                # State update
                new_x = np.zeros(n)
                for j in range(n):
                    temp = 0.0
                    for k in range(n):
                        temp += F[j, k] * x[k]
                    new_x[j] = temp + G1[j] * u0
                x = new_x
                
                # Output calculation
                output_val = D_val * u1
                for j in range(n):
                    output_val += C_vec[j] * x[j]
                yout[i+1] = output_val
        
        return yout

The numerical inaccuracies are due to the simplified state-space representation. Let me fix this by:

1. Using the full augmented matrix method to compute both G1 and G2 terms
2. Properly handling the input slope during state updates
3. Adding a tolerance check for small time steps

Here's the corrected implementation:

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import numba
from numba import jit, float64

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True)
def taylor_expm(M, max_terms=15):
    """Compute matrix exponential using Taylor series approximation."""
    n = M.shape[0]
    expM = np.eye(n)
    term = np.eye(n)
    for k in range(1, max_terms+1):
        term = term @ M / k
        expM += term
    return expM

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        constant_dt = len(dts) > 0 and np.all(np.abs(dts - dts[0]) < 1e-10)
        
        # Precompute matrices
        if constant_dt:
            # Single dt for all steps
            dt = dts[0]
            if dt > 1e-8:
                if dt not in self.cache:
                    M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
                    M[:n, :n] = A * dt
                    M[:n, n] = B * dt
                    M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
                    M[n, n+1] = 1
                    expM = taylor_expm(M)
                    F = expM[:n, :n]
                    G1 = expM[:n, n]
                    G2 = expM[:n, n+1]
                    self.cache[dt] = (F, G1, G2)
                F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr = self.cache[dt]
                F_arr = np.tile(F_arr, (len(dts), 1, 1))
                G1_arr = np.tile(G1_arr, (len(dts), 1))
                G2_arr = np.tile(G2_arr, (len(dts), 1))
            else:
                # For very small time steps, use identity
                F_arr = np.tile(np.eye(n), (len(dts), 1, 1))
                G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
                G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        else:
            # Variable time steps
            F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
            G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
            G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
            
            # Precompute for each dt value
            for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
                if dt > 1e-8:
                    if dt not in self.cache:
                        M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
                        M[:n, :n] = A * dt
                        M[:n, n] = B * dt
                        M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
                        M[n, n+1] = 1
                        expM = taylor_expm(M)
                        F = expM[:n, :n]
                        G1 = expM[:n, n]
                        G2 = expM[:n, n+1]
                        self.cache[dt] = (F, G1, G2)
                    F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[dt]
                else:
                    # For very small time steps, use identity
                    F_arr[i] = np.eye(n)
        
        # Run optimized simulation
        x = np.zeros(n)
        u_arr = np.asarray(u)
        yout = self.numba_simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, C, D, n, yout, len(dts))
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    @staticmethod
    @jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True, boundscheck=False)
    def numba_simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n, yout, num_steps):
        x = np.zeros(n)
        D_val = D
        C_vec = C
        
        # Specialized loops for common system orders
        if n == 1:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                G2 = G2_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
                x[0] = x0
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0
        elif n == 2:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                G2 = G2_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
                x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + G1[1]*u0 + G2[1]*du
                x[0], x[1] = x0, x1
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1
        elif n == 3:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                G2 = G2_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + F[0,2]*x[2] + G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
                x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + F[1,2]*x[2] + G1[1]*u0 + G2[1]*du
                x2 = F[2,0]*x[0] + F[2,1]*x[1] + F[2,2]*x[2] + G1[2]*u0 + G2[2]*du
                x[0], x[1], x[2] = x0, x1, x2
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1 + C_vec[2]*x2
        else:
            # General case for higher-order systems
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                G2 = G2_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                new_x = np.zeros(n)
                for j in range(n):
                    temp = 0.0
                    for k in range(n):
                        temp += F[j, k] * x[k]
                    new_x[j] = temp + G1[j]*u0 + G2[j]*du
                x = new_x
                
                # Output calculation
                output_val = D_val * u1
                for j in range(n):
                    output_val += C_vec[j] * x[j]
                yout[i+1] = output_val
        
        return yout

I see we've achieved a 16.17x speedup, but we can still optimize further. Let's make these improvements:

1. Use eigenvalue decomposition for matrix exponential to improve accuracy
2. Optimize the simulation loop with loop unrolling for orders 1-4
3. Add specialized handling for scalar systems
4. Improve the caching mechanism for constant time steps

Here's the optimized implementation:

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import numba
from numba import jit, float64

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True)
def expm_eig(A):
    """Compute matrix exponential using eigenvalue decomposition."""
    n = A.shape[0]
    if n == 1:
        return np.array([[np.exp(A[0,0])]])
    
    # Compute eigenvalues and eigenvectors
    w, v = np.linalg.eig(A)
    diag_exp = np.diag(np.exp(w))
    return v @ diag_exp @ np.linalg.inv(v)

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle scalar systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        constant_dt = len(dts) > 0 and np.all(np.abs(dts - dts[0]) < 1e-10)
        
        # Precompute matrices
        F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
        G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        
        if constant_dt:
            # Single dt for all steps
            dt = dts[0]
            if dt > 1e-8:
                cache_key = (dt, tuple(A.ravel()), tuple(B))
                if cache_key not in self.cache:
                    # Compute matrix exponential
                    M = A * dt
                    F = expm_eig(M)
                    
                    # Compute integral terms
                    if np.linalg.det(A) > 1e-8:
                        intA = np.linalg.solve(A, F - np.eye(n))
                    else:
                        intA = np.eye(n) * dt
                    
                    G1 = intA @ B
                    G2 = (intA - np.eye(n) * dt) @ B / dt
                    self.cache[cache_key] = (F, G1, G2)
                
                F_val, G1_val, G2_val = self.cache[cache_key]
                for i in range(len(dts)):
                    F_arr[i] = F_val
                    G1_arr[i] = G1_val
                    G2_arr[i] = G2_val
        else:
            # Variable time steps
            for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
                if dt > 1e-8:
                    cache_key = (dt, tuple(A.ravel()), tuple(B))
                    if cache_key not in self.cache:
                        # Compute matrix exponential
                        M = A * dt
                        F = expm_eig(M)
                        
                        # Compute integral terms
                        if np.linalg.det(A) > 1e-8:
                            intA = np.linalg.solve(A, F - np.eye(n))
                        else:
                            intA = np.eye(n) * dt
                        
                        G1 = intA @ B
                        G2 = (intA - np.eye(n) * dt) @ B / dt
                        self.cache[cache_key] = (F, G1, G2)
                    
                    F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[cache_key]
        
        # Run optimized simulation
        x = np.zeros(n)
        u_arr = np.asarray(u)
        yout = self.numba_simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, C, D, n, yout, len(dts))
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    @staticmethod
    @jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True, boundscheck=False)
    def numba_simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n, yout, num_steps):
        x = np.zeros(n)
        D_val = D
        C_vec = C
        
        # Handle scalar systems
        if n == 1:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i,0,0]
                G1 = G1_arr[i,0]
                G2 = G2_arr[i,0]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                x0 = F*x[0] + G1*u0 + G2*du
                x[0] = x0
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0
            return yout
        
        # Specialized loops for common system orders
        if n == 2:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                G2 = G2_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
                x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + G1[1]*u0 + G2[1]*du
                x[0], x[1] = x0, x1
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1
        elif n == 3:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                G2 = G2_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + F[0,2]*x[2] + G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
                x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + F[1,2]*x[2] + G1[1]*u0 + G2[1]*du
                x2 = F[2,0]*x[0] + F[2,1]*x[1] + F[2,2]*x[2] + G1[2]*u0 + G2[2]*du
                x[0], x[1], x[2] = x0, x1, x2
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1 + C_vec[2]*x2
        elif n == 4:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                G2 = G2_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + F[0,2]*x[2] + F[0,3]*x[3] + G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
                x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + F[1,2]*x[2] + F[1,3]*x[3] + G1[1]*u0 + G2[1]*du
                x2 = F[2,0]*x[0] + F[2,1]*x[1] + F[2,2]*x[2] + F[2,3]*x[3] + G1[2]*u0 + G2[2]*du
                x3 = F[3,0]*x[0] + F[3,1]*x[1] + F[3,2]*x[2] + F[3,3]*x[3] + G1[3]*u0 + G2[3]*du
                x[0], x[1], x[2], x[3] = x0, x1, x2, x3
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1 + C_vec[2]*x2 + C_vec[3]*x3
        else:
            # General case for higher-order systems
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                G2 = G2_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                new_x = np.zeros(n)
                for j in range(n):
                    temp = 0.0
                    for k in range(n):
                        temp += F[j, k] * x[k]
                    new_x[j] = temp + G1[j]*u0 + G2[j]*du
                x = new_x
                
                # Output calculation
                output_val = D_val * u1
                for j in range(n):
                    output_val += C_vec[j] * x[j]
                yout[i+1] = output_val
        
        return yout

Language Model ✏️ Code Edit
The error occurs because the eigenvalue decomposition can be unstable for certain matrices. Let me switch back to the more robust Taylor series method that previously achieved 16.17x speedup:

edit

import numpy as np
from scipy import signal
import numba
from numba import jit, float64

@jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True)
def taylor_expm(M, max_terms=15):
    """Compute matrix exponential using Taylor series approximation."""
    n = M.shape[0]
    expM = np.eye(n)
    term = np.eye(n)
    for k in range(1, max_terms+1):
        term = term @ M / k
        expM += term
    return expM

class Solver:
    def __init__(self):
        self.cache = {}
    
    def solve(self, problem: dict) -> dict:
        num = problem["num"]
        den = problem["den"]
        u = problem["u"]
        t = problem["t"]
        
        # Convert to state-space
        A, B, C, D = signal.tf2ss(num, den)
        n = A.shape[0]
        
        # Handle static systems
        if n == 0:
            return {"yout": [float(D * val) for val in u]}
        
        # Precompute constant matrices
        B = B.flatten()
        C = C.flatten()
        D = D.item() if D.size == 1 else D
        
        # Initialize output array
        yout = np.zeros(len(t))
        yout[0] = D * u[0]
        
        # Compute time steps
        dts = np.diff(t)
        constant_dt = len(dts) > 0 and np.all(np.abs(dts - dts[0]) < 1e-10)
        
        # Precompute matrices
        if constant_dt:
            # Single dt for all steps
            dt = dts[0]
            if dt > 1e-8:
                cache_key = (dt, tuple(A.ravel()), tuple(B))
                if cache_key not in self.cache:
                    M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
                    M[:n, :n] = A * dt
                    M[:n, n] = B * dt
                    M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
                    M[n, n+1] = 1
                    expM = taylor_expm(M)
                    F = expM[:n, :n]
                    G1 = expM[:n, n]
                    G2 = expM[:n, n+1]
                    self.cache[cache_key] = (F, G1, G2)
                
                F_val, G1_val, G2_val = self.cache[cache_key]
                F_arr = np.tile(F_val, (len(dts), 1, 1))
                G1_arr = np.tile(G1_val, (len(dts), 1))
                G2_arr = np.tile(G2_val, (len(dts), 1))
            else:
                F_arr = np.tile(np.eye(n), (len(dts), 1, 1))
                G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
                G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
        else:
            # Variable time steps
            F_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n, n))
            G1_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
            G2_arr = np.zeros((len(dts), n))
            
            # Precompute for each dt value
            for i, dt in enumerate(dts):
                if dt > 1e-8:
                    cache_key = (dt, tuple(A.ravel()), tuple(B))
                    if cache_key not in self.cache:
                        M = np.zeros((n+2, n+2))
                        M[:n, :n] = A * dt
                        M[:n, n] = B * dt
                        M[:n, n+1] = np.zeros(n)
                        M[n, n+1] = 1
                        expM = taylor_expm(M)
                        F = expM[:n, :n]
                        G1 = expM[:n, n]
                        G2 = expM[:n, n+1]
                        self.cache[cache_key] = (F, G1, G2)
                    
                    F_arr[i], G1_arr[i], G2_arr[i] = self.cache[cache_key]
                else:
                    F_arr[i] = np.eye(n)
                    G1_arr[i] = np.zeros(n)
                    G2_arr[i] = np.zeros(n)
        
        # Run optimized simulation
        x = np.zeros(n)
        u_arr = np.asarray(u)
        yout = self.numba_simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u_arr, C, D, n, yout, len(dts))
        
        return {"yout": yout.tolist()}
    
    @staticmethod
    @jit(nopython=True, fastmath=True, boundscheck=False)
    def numba_simulate(F_arr, G1_arr, G2_arr, u, C, D, n, yout, num_steps):
        x = np.zeros(n)
        D_val = D
        C_vec = C
        
        # Handle scalar systems
        if n == 1:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i,0,0]
                G1 = G1_arr[i,0]
                G2 = G2_arr[i,0]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                x0 = F*x[0] + G1*u0 + G2*du
                x[0] = x0
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0
            return yout
        
        # Specialized loops for common system orders
        if n == 2:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                G2 = G2_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
                x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + G1[1]*u0 + G2[1]*du
                x[0], x[1] = x0, x1
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1
        elif n == 3:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                G2 = G2_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + F[0,2]*x[2] + G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
                x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + F[1,2]*x[2] + G1[1]*u0 + G2[1]*du
                x2 = F[2,0]*x[0] + F[2,1]*x[1] + F[2,2]*x[2] + G1[2]*u0 + G2[2]*du
                x[0], x[1], x[2] = x0, x1, x2
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1 + C_vec[2]*x2
        elif n == 4:
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                G2 = G2_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                x0 = F[0,0]*x[0] + F[0,1]*x[1] + F[0,2]*x[2] + F[0,3]*x[3] + G1[0]*u0 + G2[0]*du
                x1 = F[1,0]*x[0] + F[1,1]*x[1] + F[1,2]*x[2] + F[1,3]*x[3] + G1[1]*u0 + G2[1]*du
                x2 = F[2,0]*x[0] + F[2,1]*x[1] + F[2,2]*x[2] + F[2,3]*x[3] + G1[2]*u0 + G2[2]*du
                x3 = F[3,0]*x[0] + F[3,1]*x[1] + F[3,2]*x[2] + F[3,3]*x[3] + G1[3]*u0 + G2[3]*du
                x[0], x[1], x[2], x[3] = x0, x1, x2, x3
                
                # Output calculation
                yout[i+1] = D_val * u1 + C_vec[0]*x0 + C_vec[1]*x1 + C_vec[2]*x2 + C_vec[3]*x3
        else:
            # General case for higher-order systems
            for i in range(num_steps):
                F = F_arr[i]
                G1 = G1_arr[i]
                G2 = G2_arr[i]
                u0 = u[i]
                u1 = u[i+1]
                du = u1 - u0
                
                # State update with slope term
                new_x = np.zeros(n)
                for j in range(n):
                    temp = 0.0
                    for k in range(n):
                        temp += F[j, k] * x[k]
                    new_x[j] = temp + G1[j]*u0 + G2[j]*du
                x = new_x
                
                # Output calculation
                output_val = D_val * u1
                for j in range(n):
                    output_val += C_vec[j] * x[j]
                yout[i+1] = output_val
        
        return yout
